text:
Here are few tips that I learn from doing that recipe. First, I tripled most of the recipe, except for the topping. I baked it into big rectangular corning ware dish (about 16" x 9). I added a touch of almond extract. It gives it a nice taste. When baked, I topped it with a touch of icing sugar. It looked great. DO NOT over cook. I baked them for 30-35 minutes. These squares are better when they are moist. Do as the recipe says. Do not use a toothpick to judge if bake or not as it will come out as if it was not baked. Hope this help!

text:
I took these to work and everyone loved them! I doubled the recipe and baked them in a 9X13 pan instead so they were thicker, more like cake. I also used less brown sugar than it called for (because I ran out) and substituted with extra white sugar, and I used pecans instead of walnuts. It turned out great! The only thing I would do differently--if doubling the recipe in one pan again, I wouldn't double the cinnamon sugar topping because there was way too much. I used it all and when the bars were picked up, tons fell off---mostly sugar, leaving a VERY strong cinnamon taste, probably more than many people would want.

text:
Just made these this afternoon and the kids had already eaten half the pan before the bars finished cooling!  These are really tasty.  I doubled the recipe (but I cut down BOTH sugars to approx. 3/4c each) and increased the apples to 2 large chopped apples (just over 2c).  Left out the nuts.  The bars were still sweet enough and don't require any frosting (although the caramel drizzle one reviewer suggested would be delish).  Did not double the cinn/sugar topping.  Baked in 9x13 pan for 33 minutes.  My daughter said to save this recipe and we'll definitely make again soon!

text:
I didn't try these so I have to write this review based on Hubs' report. He said these were the kind of thing he could eat till he got sick on they were that good. Five stars, he said, and better than his all-time favorite butterscotch cookies. Wow! I used Granny Smith apple, left out the nuts at his request and glazed them (right on top of the cinnamon sugar topping) with a butterscotch glaze I kind of just threw together as an experiment: 2 T. each of butter, brown sugar and cream, boiled for a couple of minutes, added about 1/2 tsp. vanilla, then more cream and powdered sugar till desired consistency.  These are chewy, subtley cinnamony and appley with a butterscotch finish (his words, not mine). Definitely a make again!

text:
I made this recipe 3 times in the last couple of days.  I had bought apples in bulk and needed to use them.  I made 2 recipes with a 9x9 pan, cutting both sugars down to less than 1/2 cup each.  The first time, I used 1 cup of apples but the next time, I used 1 1/2 full apples and I liked it better with more apples.  With more apples, the squares are more moist and cakey.  I also made a batch in a 9x13 pan -- I doubled the recipe, used 3/4 cup of each sugar, used 2 1/2 full apples, and baked for 33 minutes.  No need to double the sugar topping.  Delicious!  And I had all the ingredients in my pantry already.  This is going to be one of my favorite recipes.

text:
I have made these several times now and thought that it was about time that I put my review in.  These are wonderful!! Everytime that I make them they disappear quickly.  I use 1 and a 1/2 times the recipe and bake in a 13'X 9' pan. Then I put a carmel glaze drizzled over the top. Just put powdered sugar (about 1/2 to 3/4 Cup)in a small bowl with enough milk to make a semi-thin glaze and stir a couple of tablespoonsfull of the carmel used for dipping apples etc.(Found in the produce section of your market). Drizzle over the top.

text:
Love this basis of this recipie but I did tweek it the second time.  I made the first batch exactly as specified and would rate it a 3.5, mainly because it was too sugary for me and not enough apples.   Second batch was  5 stars, here's what i did: I doubled most of the ingredients and used 5 nice size apples (about 2 1/2 cups) and added 1/2 cup apple juice.  I also cut down on the sugar, using just 1/2 cup brown, 1/2 cup white.  It turned out less sugary, moist and delicious!  The second time I didn't even finish by sprinkling the cinnamon and sugar on top - the family didn't even notice!  They've been begging for more apple brownies ever since.

Really moist and gooey.  I doubled the recipe too, except for the sugar and cinnamon topping. For the sugar, I used only 1 cup brown sugar, 1/4 cup white sugar and it was plenty sweet.  Next time, I think I'll add about 1/2 cup apple juice for more apple flavor and tang.  I will also use Granny Smith and double the apples. I used a braeburn apple this time and the flavor was too flat.  I doubled the recipe but still used a 9x9 dish and baked exactly 40 min.  Like a gooey coffee cake. Just make sure to cool completely before cutting since the cake is so moist.  Will make again.  (I gave only 4 star since it wasn't 100% perfect. Doubling the apples is a must!)

text:
I wish I would have doubled the batter recipe, not the cinnamon and sugar topping quantity.  This was a tease! If you are going to try this, double it. Don't double the cinnamon and sugar topping. I used 1 teas cinnamon, 1 tablespoon of white and brown sugar for the topping. I baked it for 35 mins til bars sprung back when touched. I noticed the squares were crumbly, it was a little salty and dry--------Mar 07th, 2011. I made these again last night. I doubled the recipe this time. I accidentally added baking soda instead of baking powder. I left the soda in and added baking powder too, so 1 teas of soda and 1 teas powder. I think it was a good mistake. I added 2 full cups of chopped apples and squeezed a wedge of lemon over them. I didn't need to double the topping amount by last experience. I baked it for about 55 mins in my small oven. It was hard to let it cool, it smelled so good. The first bite was heaven and it got better from there. It was crunchy on the outside and soft and apple-y on the inside, melts in your mouth delight. My family couldn't stop eating. This is the best apple/cake/squares ever. It was all gone in less than 24 hours. When I woke up at midnight, there were 6 pieces out of 12 left, went back to bed. Woke up again at 8am, 4 pieces left. After work NONE left. Lol... This is one of my favorite recipes now, thank you for sharing. It was OK the first time but irresistible the second time. It gets better and better!

text:
Heavenly. I followed some users advices, and done some changes of my own: 1/3 cup white sugar, 1/3 cup brown sugar, 1 ts cinnamon for the topping, double the whole recipe because it serves only 12 very small squares, unless you're doing it for 2 people only :). it's taste is even better the next day. I've used a fruit dip recipe (this site) to make diagonal lines over the squares, for the amount mentioned above (original recipe) just mix 4 ounce of cream cheese, 1/4 cup brown sugar, 1/2 tsp vanilla, and pipe it on the squares diagonally (cut the squares before you put the topping). Hope this will help you, it did for me :)

text:
These are delicious! I went apple picking and was searching for a non-pie apple recipe. This is a very quick, tasty dish. I made it for my husband to bring to a tailgating party and it got rave reviews. I made another one with the leftover apples I had towards the end of my apple supply. I added much more apples than the recipe calls for. I used 6 small empire apples. I also topped it with 1 Tbspn of brown sugar and 1 Tbspn of white sugar instead of all white sugar. There is a bit too much of the sugar topping. The first time I made it I put it all on top and the result was a lot of loose sugar on top when you bite into them. The second time I made them I only sprinkled a little to cover and threw the rest out. Next time I make them I will drizzle a little melted butter over the top too in order to solidify the topping.

I have made this recipe 3 times now.. and we love it!  The first time, it was undercooked.. the middle was doughy.  The second time, it was overcooked and the sides were quite hard.  The third time.. it was PERFECT!  It was a huge hit and everyone was raving about!   Pay attention to the time that the apple squares are in the oven.. it is very very important.  I did double the recipe and the only thing I changed.. omitted the nuts (not a nut fan) and tripled the apples - used Gala apples.  Chopped up the apples a pretty fine size.  Made the apple squares so good.  Also, dont need as much cinnamon / sugar on top as the recipe called for. Definite keeper.. will make this recipe over and over again - soo incredibly good!

I don't think I've ever been more pleased with a new recipe!  I used whole wheat flour instead of regular ~ because that's all I use ~ and doubled the recipe and baked it in a 9x13 inch cake pan, as others have.  I have a 16 year old son who's IMPOSSIBLE and won't eat nuts in anything, so I decided to forgo the walnuts and added extra apple ~ for the doubled recipe, I used 1 and 1/2 cups Fuji apples (GREAT this year here in MI).  I was also out of cinnamon, so I used 1/8 teaspoon cloves and 1/2 teaspoon ginger instead. And I used just a tablespoon of white sugar with a couple of pinches of cloves and ginger sprinkled on top before baking.  WOW! My son LOVES it!  I LOVE it! When you can tweak a recipe and have the result turn out amazingly, the recipe in itself is great.  This is great!

These were fantastic! -- but with a few modifications.  I took the advice of many and doubled the recipe and baked it in a 9x13 pan. I also cut down on the sugar and was so glad that I did.  I used 3/4 of a cup of each sugar for a double recipe and it was plenty sweet. I also upped the apples and used 2 very large apples (I used Jonagold - it's a sweet apple). I baked it 33 minutes at 350 and it was perfect. I brought this to a function and it was the star of the night.  :)

text:
I used one whole green tart apple, it was probably the size of a softball.  I did not peel it, just cored and diced into the batter.  I'm sure it was more than 1/2 c of apple.  The batter was made as is except reducing the white sugar to 1/4 c since most reviewers said it was too sweet.  I added a small amount of nutmeg too.  The batter was very thick when trying to add in the apples so I added about 1 T of apple juice.  The topping seemed heavy on cinnamon so I only used 1/2 t.  The squares were very delicious.  I will make again.  I really think you need to use sour apples for this or it would be entirely too sweet.

text:
Well,  must say first off that I failed when making this recipe. To start off with I didn't have a 9x9 pan, so I used an 8x8. (That was mistake number one.) I didn't have brown sugar, so I used a cup of white. (That actually worked)I mixed it all as instructed and baked it. It came out looking great! (Apart from the fact that the cinnamon/sugar mixture on top just looked like raw cinnamon and sugar on top.)The middle sunk a little after cooling.So this is where my fail actually takes place. I envisioned a nice bubbly crust on top, kinda like you might see on a nice creme brule (sp?) Well not having a food grade blow torch I turn on the broiler and set the apple bars in. I stood there knowing it shouldn't take long. After a few minutes I open the oven to find FLAMES!!! I snatch out the flaming apple goodness and blow it out FAST. I stand there staring at what looks like a charcoal briquet. My heart has sunk to my toes. I decide to try and pick off the scorched top and was happy to find it was just the cinnamon/sugar mixture that was ruined!! The rest just turned out to taste like a nice moist apple cake. It tasted really good! If not for my total failure it may have just tasted great! I think I will try this recipe again without catching it on fire.

text:
The 1st time I made this I used an 8" square pan.  They turned out 'gushy' but we ate them warm with vanilla ice cream. The second time in a 9" pan I only used 1/2 the cinnamon sugar topping, because it seemed too much.  They were great, very tasty and good texture. I decided to try them a 3rd time with the full amount of topping so I could fairly review this recipe. They turned out very well, but I don't think that there was any benefit to the additional cinnamon sugar. This recipe makes a square with the texture like a brownie.  Adding more apples would change that.  Also, if you double the recipe , it should be baked in a 10"x15" pan rather than a 9"x13" as it's closer in square inches. I just made my double batch in 2- 9" square pans. They were a big hit. I used a Granny Smith apple.

text:
This has become a breakfast staple in my house replacing pop-tarts and cereal bars. My girls also like to take them in their lunch for a treat. I triple the recipe, leave out the nuts and leave off the cinnamon/sugar topping. I bake in 2 9x13 pans and cut each pan into 18 bars. After they cool I layer them in an airtight container and freeze them. In the morning the girls heat them for 30 seconds in the microwave and they are wonderful. If they take one in their lunch it is thawed by lunch time. They are great to have on hand when the girls bring friends home too!

This recipe was wonderful!  I tasty way to use extra apples.  I am only giving this 4 stars because I made two batches of these and both were a little dry for my taste.  My first batch I followed the recipe exactly, and those were considerably more moist than the second batch.  On my second batch I did not have any nuts in the house, so I substituted the same amount of old-fashioned oats in its place.  And I drizzled some honey over the top before baking in addition to the cinnamon and sugar.  Those bars were more cake-like and much more dry.  I ended up glazing both batches with a simple powdered sugar glaze to moisten them up.  They were delicious!  I will be making these again, that's for sure!

text:
I made a lot of changes, but the base-recipe was so good I still felt it deserved a high rating.  I used 3/4 cup white spelt flour and 1/4 cup oats in place of the full 1 cup flour, 1/4 cup melted Smart Balance Light in place of the butter, 1/2 cup packed brown sugar plus 3 packets of stevia (no white sugar was necessary!), 1/2 tsp. cinammon in place of 1/4, pecans instead of apples and an entire large apple in place of the 1/2 cup.  I also added 1/4 cup all natural apple juice to the batter and drizzled a dairy-free caramel-sauce over the top (omitted the specified sugar and cinnamon at the end).  I baked it for the specified time in a standard tart-pan, and it was incredible--easily the best apple-dessert I've ever served.  Thank you so much for the great base to work with!

I bake for seniors groups. I try to do something different every week. This week I choose these apple squares. I am sorry I did. I am on a diet and I had a tiny little piece and could have eaten the entire 9 x 13 pan. They are absolutely delicious and so easy to make. The ladies don't like nuts (dentures you know) and I didn't have any raisins to I added the last of my currants and it turned out great. Can hardly wait to see their reaction at tomorrow's meeting. I hope I managed to keep my hands off them until then. Thanks so much for a wonderful recipe. Oh I took others advice, doubled the recipe, used only 1/2 c of brown sugar and 1/2 of Splendid and used 3 Pacific Rose apples with skin still on. Just sprinkled about 1.5 T of brown sugar on top and pressed it in so it wouldn't fall off. Forgot to mention also next time I would triple the recipe as they came out a little on the thin side and the 'girls' like a good mouthful.

This is a good recipe.  I made it one day, 1 1/2 times the recipe in a 9 x 13" pan.  I backed the sugar up by about a third and halved the topping, all based on other people's reviews.  The result was good enough that we wanted more but seemed to be missing something, so I made another batch.  One and a half times the recipe in a 9" x 13" pan, with full bore sugar. Lots of classic flavors here, especially when you put a square of it in a bowl and pour some cream in beside it.  Sometimes you just need all the sugar.  Thank you.

Looking for something to do on a snowy day while my wife was out and saw this recipe.  My wife and I recently picked two bushels of Northern Spy apples and I was looking for a good apple recipe. I did not use the last two ingredients as I thought there was enough sugar in the recipe without the topping.  I followed the recipe but used a full large diced apple instead of a half cup. Didn't have a 9x9 pan so I used a 7x11 pan figuring this was close enough to the 81 sq. in. pan.  Next time I make this I will double the recipe as we ate this to quickly.

text:
Made it tonight for a Thanksgiving party. Really tasty! I love apples and this reminded me of a very similar recipe that my mom used to make. I doubled the recipe like most of the other reviewers, cut the sugar in half, used 4 gala apples, shredded instead of chopped(will increase to 5 next time) and I squeezed most of the juice out, also ground walnuts ,used baking soda instead of baking powder(always works better for me). Baked in a 9x13 dish and it came out very fluffy and not too sweet, more like apple bread(I like that!) skipped the sugar on top, only used cinnamon and after cooled and cut, I sprinkled vanilla powder sugar(home made for x-mas cookies). It's the only topping fine enough to stick, as I noticed some of the comments posted that sugar was falling off. Will make again:)

I had high hopes for these but they were just average for us.  Made them as stated except I used twice the amount of apples and went a little skimpy when measuring  the sugars, as suggested by others.  They were really hard to spread in the pan and turned out pretty thin.  The topping was way too much and I even left some in the bowl because it looked like too much.  I did drizzle them with a basic powdered sugar icing (which added a nice touch).  I sent these to a potluck without trying them, based on the great reviews, and I am so regretful now.  With all the great bar recipes out there, I will definitely not be making these again.

text:
These turned out so delicious! I made with the written amounts of sugars and these were very sweet. Personally I will cut each down to 1/4c in the future but that's a matter of preference; as written these are still yummy. I also used two chopped Gala apples, which came out to at least a cup and a half. This made a very fruity moist bar, which we loved. I would use half a cup if I needed a bar that was more resilient, with all the apple I used you couldn't really pick one up and munch it. The batter is stiff, I plopped it into the pan and had to use my fingers to spread it out. I look forward to making these all fall, thanks so much for sharing!

text:
Love these!!! After reading all the negative reviews, I was kindda skeptical, BUT! It turned out PERFECT with: 1-) Triple recipe  2-) Use only 1 cup of brown sugar 3-) Increase to 4 Large apples cooked first with 1/2 lemon and 1/2 cup water for 10 min on boil so that the water evaporates a bit. 5-) Sprinkle with 2 Tbs sugar + 2 tsp ground cinnamon. LAST bake in 9x13 glass dish at 175C for 45min. MOIST but holding together :) I also tried it with 2 cup of AP flour + 1 cup of whole wheat flour and the consistency is even more brownie like PLUS more healthy! :)

I made these for a get together with my friends yesterday and they were fantastic!!!

I didn't use nut because I didn't have any so I up the amount to about a cup (1 large granny smith). Once we tasted them we decide we would continue making them without the nuts. I also used an 8.5 X 11 pan because that's what I had.

I know some of the other reviews said the cinnamon sugar feel of the top of the bars. I avoided this by just gently patting the topping into the top of the bars before baking. I didn't reduce the topping amounts because we love cinnamon!!

I will make these again and again!! Thank you for the wonderful recipe!!

-I think I used 3 C apples.  I filled a 2C measure till the top & kept going!  I chopped the apples; next time I'll see what dicing it would do.
-I toasted the walnuts, then did a med-fine chop.  
--I have family members that can't have chocolate, so this is a great recipe to bring to get-togethers!
--Thank you so very much for sharing this recipe!  My hubby was happy to share it at work & I had enough to give to friends, too.  I'm definitely 
making this again!
--I gave it 5 stars 'cause it helped bring smiles!

text:
I am giving this 4 stars for the exact recipe but 5 after the minor changes I made. For the original recipe pan size, I increased the apples to 1 cup, reduced the white & brown sugars to 1/4 cup each and added 1/2 cup sour cream. For the topping I used: 1/4 brown sugar, 1 TBS butter, 1/2 tsp. cinnamon, 1/4 cup chopped nuts (optional). Cut the cold butter into the sugar & cinnamon then add the nuts. Add topping then bake. You won't have the problem of sugar falling off the top of the squares with this method. I tried one person's suggestion of a powdered sugar glaze & that was a hit. Next time I will try a butterscotch/caramel glaze. However, these apple squares are wonderful without the additional glazes...just a way to make the recipe a little different.

This was awesome!!!  A 9X13 pan PLUM & apple version of this just came out of my oven at 3 pm & now, 40 minutes later, half the pan is gone!  Even my daughter- who doesn't like cooked fruit- is eating it up!  Why plums? Well, I had 2 lbs of too-sour apples that I was GOING to use for this recipe, went to find the apples this morning for this recipe- and only AFTER I had started the recipe (thinking I had all the ingredients needed) did I find my husband had forced himself to eat them all week because no one else would! Made these today as I had a bunch of wind blown apples in our garden. Read several reviews and decided to double the recipe (excluding the topping). YUM! This is exactly what I was looking for. These bars were pretty easy to make...it's the day after I made them and the pan of them is almost gone already! I definitely should have doubled the recipe. The only changes I made were to use 1 cup instead of 1/2 cup of chopped apples. I also took the other's advice, and added 1/4 tsp. almond extract. I baked for 25 minutes, and they came out perfect. The cinnamon-sugar topping made a little too much, so I wouldn't make so much next time. The only thing that was a bit tricky, is that the bars were a little hard to keep in a bar shape when I went to take them out of the pan, not a big deal though- just required some being careful.  The consistency is great, not too dense, not too light. Definitely a keeper.

text:
OMG, I loved this recipe.  I did tweak it a bit.  I doubled the recipe since I used a 13x9 pan. I read some reviews, and ended up putting 2 cups of apples into the bars.  I did at some nutmeg just to have something extra.  I also put in around a teaspoon more of vanilla because why not? Lastly, I added almond milk to the recipe.  After cooking for around 30 minutes, the bars came out fantastic, and were reminiscent of coffee cake, much to the enjoyment of my family.  Also, for the topping, I just played it by sight.  I poured a little cinnamon in a bowl and a little more sugar and mixed.  After pouring the topping on top, I would make more depending on how covered the top of the dessert was.  All in all, it was amazing, and am definitely stashing this recipe away.

text:
I can't rate this on the exact recipe. I read a lot of reviews for this and tried my best to follow their suggestions. Many suggested to double the recipe except for the sugars. Now, little fact, I always half recipes when I first try them out. I don't want to waste my ingredients for a failure you know? So Instead, I used the regular recipe and decreased the sugars from 1/2 cup to 1/3 (i am sure many hear would suggest 1/4 but I have a giant sweet tooth) and double the apples from 1/2 cup to a whole one. That is what I did. Now, I was expecting more of an apple crumble consistency, this was more of a cake. But as the recipe is, it is delicious. I made these for my mom and her friends and they loved it. I made these along side with some very tasty lemon bars (also from this site) and these ran out quick. They said the apples were baked perfectly and it was just the right amount of sweetness.They bashfully reached for seconds and thirds and I was very happy they enjoyed. I liked them as well and will definitely reach for this recipe during the holidays!

My boyfriend and I made this recipe a few times, and after following the recipe exactly the first time we made a few adjustments. The first time it tasted fine, but the squares were not quite as firm as I'd expected--it seemed rather soft, so soft that when I cut into it the squares merely fell apart and I ended up eating them with a fork. (He didn't mind, however--he likes his baked sweets somewhat under-baked.) the second time we increased the baking time, and used the whole recipe in two separate baking dishes. It turned out a little better, but not as much as I'd hoped. If we do make this one again I may have to experiment to get it to come out the way I'd like it to. Overall the taste is great--I would try not to do anything to change that--but it doesn't hold together very well.

text:
This was my first time trying these and they were delicious! Our family recently picked some apples from a mountain close to our town and I could not decide on what to make. I read some of the previous reviews and tried some of the adjustments. I doubled the recipe but left the sugar amount the same, and baked it in a 9x13 pan. Others said not to double the cinnamon but I (accidentally) did anyway and it still came out great. I used 2 large Fuji apples instead, since that's what we had.  I had planned on using chopped almonds, as one member suggested, but figured I'd leave them out and take my chances. I also added about 1/3 cup of apple juice to give it more of an apple flavor. I left out the top coating of sugar and cinnamon because I didn't want it to be too sweet, and because others said it fell off too easily anyway. Let me tell you, I'm not a huge fan of apple desserts (I made these for my husband's co-workers), but these were AMAZING. I was going to drizzle some caramel on top but they were perfect without it! After cooling I cut them into squares and they didn't cut neatly, but that's perfectly fine by me. I had no problem getting a fork and going to town on all the delicious crumbs in the pan. It pretty much came out like an apple pie cake. I'll definitely have to make more sooner than expected.

I have got to say that this recipe was awesome. I thought that 1/2 cup of apples was not enough so I put in 3 medium sized apples. With this amount it was perfect. There was enough to ensure that great apple taste and that everybody had some. For the topping I accidentally used 2 TBS cinnamon instead of tsp. Got to say that the finish product was just as great. My family loved it. My one brother loves apple and when I gave him 2 pieces he asked for more unknowingly that he already ate 2! One thing that is important when making these, is to make sure that it is not hot. Maybe stick it in the fridge. Also egg replacer works well. Not as well as a regular egg but still good. Will definitely make these again and again. A truly simple dessert.

These were delicious and gone in a flash.  I even doubled the recipe!:)  Anyway, I doubled everything except the topping and baked in a 9x13 pan.  It took about 34minutes or so in the oven. For dietary reasons, I made a lot of adjustments to this recipe, but the bars were quite tasty (and I credit that to the original recipe, and some suggestions of other reviewrs, not my changes). I doubled the recipe and used a 13x9 pan. Added 1/2 tsp of cinnamon instead of 1/4, only used 2 Tbsp butter, and added 1/4 c. applesauce and 1 small, mashed banana. Only used 1/4 c. of both brown and white sugar, per other reviewer's recommendations, and doubled the amount of apple.  I did keep the topping amounts as noted, since I'd cut the sugar in the base recipe.  These wen't over really well with the kids as well as adults!  (Really loved eating them warmed, too.)

text:
The first time I saw this I just had to try it. After reading past reviewers suggestions I decided to double the recipe except for the brown and white sugar which I kept at 3/4 cup each. I used two granny smith apples and it ended up a little over 2 cups, diced. I used 2T of white sugar and 2 tsp of cinnamon topping. The topping was a nice cinnamony, sugary crunchy texture. Loved it and there was just enough flavoring throughout the squares. I've made this a couple of times and my family said these taste just like "French Apple Pie," and like it much better with the Fuji apples -vs- Granny Smith. They also said that the Fuji apples have a mellow flavor and a firmer bite. They like biting into the small apple pieces which I think adds a nice texture to the squares.   Next time I think I will serve this warm with a scoop of cold french vanilla ice cream. Ono!

Wow! These were delicious!The football team raided these and they were gone within minutes!  I was asked to make a dessert for my sons football team for their dinner on Thursday night, so I made these. I read the other reviews. I doubled the batch, add a 1/4 tsp of almond extract, put in a 13X9 pan and baked for 33 min. Perfect! I also drizzled a glaze on top, although not necessary, they are perfect they way they are! My glaze consisted of  1 cup of 10x sugar, 1/4 tsp almond extract, 2 TBSP of milk. I drizzled over bars, let it "set" and I got so many requests for the recipe! Even from the Moms the following day at the game! Made me these tonight for my honey, he will be pleasantly surprised! Definitely a keeper! Thanks BarbiAnn!

These were VERY good.  I made some healthy changes to this recipe and it was still delicious.  Here are my changes  -Half white flour/half wheat -1TBSP milled flax+ 3 tbsp water mixed well replacing the egg (we were out) -one whole small apple, diced small which was a heaping half cup, rather than just a half cup. -replaced white sugar with half white sugar half Splenda. -pecans instead of walnuts  The batter was VERY dry when mixed like cookie dough consistency (probably because of my flax substitute) so I added a few splashes of white grape juice that we happened to have in the fridge.  Baked at 350 for about 30 min.    The problem now, is that I've eaten 3 of them.  Defeats the purpose of the healthy changes!

These were great. I took them to work and within 15 minutes the pan was gone (and there are only about 10 people in the office). 

I doubled the recipe & put in 9x13 pan (they got about an inch thick). Also, took advice of others and doubled apples (2 cups) and left the topping at the original amount. Would also be great served warm with ice cream or made with rhubarb instead (have to try that in the spring). I'll definitely be making these again in the next day or so. Thanks!

text:
I reviewed this recipe a while back and gave it about 4, maybe 4 and a half stars.  I went back to this recipe and after re-doing it, I give it 5 stars all around.  I made some ingredient adjustments but kept the 'main theme' of the dessert right in line with the recipe.  I used large apples which was probably double the 1/2 cup called for.  And this time I actually cooked the apples on the stove top before adding to the 'cake' batter.  I added a little lemon juice, water, cinnamon, and a pinch of salt to the apples and made kind an apple pie type of filling.  This helped the apples bake right and become super moist.  I also added 1/4 of applesauce and some nutmeg along with the cinnamon.  I did not have walnuts on hand and had to leave them out.  Then I doubled everything, including my own changes, and baked in a 1/4 sheet cake pan, leaving off the cinnamon sugar topping.  And instead I used a vanilla glaze recipe from this site, just adding in a pinch of cinnamon.  These bars were so incredible moist and yummy.  Definitely more of a cake bar, but not quite a cake if that makes sense?  Either way, very yummy.  Will be making this over and over and over!

text:
I was pretty happy with the end result, but after reading other reviews, I, like many others, made some changes to the original recipe. I decided to make a double batch, so I doubled everything except for the sugars - I only used 3/4 cup of each. I increased the apples to 3 cups, but next time I think I would use at least 4 cups for the double batch. I think that in the future I might add some oatmeal as well. I also added 1/4 cup of apple juice, and instead of doing the cinammon sugar topping, I did a streusel topping of 2 Tbsp flour, 1/4 cup brown sugar, 1 tsp cinammon, and 2 Tbsp cold butter. The streusel wasn't very impressive, though, so I ended up topping the bars with cream cheese frosting and then sprinkling them with cinammon. The bars stuck to the pan (even though I greased it) and crumbled some, but they ended up tasting pretty good.

I give it 5 stars after the changes.  I used the most popular/helpful review for a jumpoff point.  The size pan I had available is 10x15x1/1/2 cookie sheet (lined w/ parchment paper).  I tripled the dough recipe (expect for the sugar-- I used  c of white and brown sugar).  I chopped 4 good sized apples (2 granny smith and 1 braeburn and 1 gala) That's about 4 cups of chopped apples.  I did not season these.  Next time I will season w/ cinnamon, a bit of sugar, nutmeg, allspice and bit of lemon juice so the bars won't be so bland tasting.  I only used little cinn/sugar topping per other reviewers suggestions. I followed the basic method for combining ingredients. Smooth out in the pan.  Try checking as early as 20 min for the proper cooking time.  It should just sping back when you touch it.  One reviewer described these as "apple brownies"  --that's pretty accurate.  Holds in refrigerator in a plastic container for days and-- moist and still a bit cakey-  still taste great.

country:

text:
I have made these squares for everyone I know (they become OBSESSED & ask me to make them a pan haha) so I consider myself an expert! I have made them as-is, wi/o nuts, w/pecans, as a vegan dish (sub 1/8c cinn. applesauce per 1egg, 3/4c olive oil sub milk OR use same amount coconut milk or rice milk) but the secret ingredient, hands down, is cinnamon applesauce. When I first made the recipe (as-is) I had to add an addtl egg because mixture looked dry. The addtl egg did add moisture but squares were still a tad too dry. Not a lot but just enough that my family noticed. The next time I made them, I subbed 1/4c cinn. applesauce for the 2eggs & that did improve the moisture somewhat. Also, I didn't care for the texture of chopped apples so I switched that to grated. I kept tweaking it slightly every time I made them & now, my literal 10th time making them, I finally have a mix that I'm personally very happy with! It's not radically different from the original recipe (the original is AMAZING & I thank the poster for this!) but here is what has worked best for me: Double entire recipe for 11x9 pan, Use heaping TSP of cinn. in dry mix, Use 1/4c cinn. applesauce in place of two eggs. Use heaping TSP of vanilla extract, add 1/8c cinn. applesauce to batter once dry & wet is mixed, grate apples w/large grater (looks like shredded cheese), fold apples into combined mix. Mix should look like cake batter w/some texture. I baked at 350 for full 30mins and it was PERFECT. A new fave :)

text:
We loved it! I doubled the recipe and then doubled the cinnamon, so it was more of a cake than a bar. It took 40-45 mins. to fully bake. I substituted coconut oil for butter, and substituted half brown sugar and half powdered sugar instead of white sugar (because I don't buy it.) Instead of the topping suggested by the recipe, I made a butterscotch drizzle with 2T. coconut oil, 2T. brown sugar and 2T. cream, brought to a boil for 1-2 mins. then added 1t. vanilla. Added powdered sugar and whole milk until desired consistency and let sit for half hour to thicken while the cake cooled.

I altered the recipe per other's advice,  but my review is based off how it should've turned out...not the way mine did.  I guess this is a lesson:  if you alter the original recipe, use your common sense a bit.  I added maybe 3 c of apple (everyone said more).  Of course I had doubled the recipe, but with that much apple, I had to make another half portion of just batter.  Now I'm putting it in my pyrex dish...by the way, no one mentions how difficult the batter was to mix in with the apples/walnuts...and set the oven, and don't check back til 30min post.  At that point, the exterior is a gorgeous just past gold, but the middle does not look set.  I put it in for another 10min.  Now the exterior is more brown, and it looks ok enough to take out.  Unfortunately, once cooled, the middle was still barely solid.   I did try a corner piece which was nice and crunchy and good.  But back into the oven for the rest of it, this time covered in foil for another 30...Anyways, the end product led someone to ask me if I had tried to steam the cake to make it healthier.  What?   Hindsight and all, I should've baked lower and slower.  If there is a next time, I'll be sure to watch it more closely.

text:
Love this recipe. I doubled the recipe each time using a 9 X 13 pan. The first time I made it exactly as posted and it was delicious. The second time I made one small change. I added the apples & walnuts to the wet mix and then added the flour mixture. It was much easier to mix and made no difference to the delicious outcome. I had a bushel of apples to use up so I'm making Apple Crisp, Apple Sauce,  I made 4 trays of the Apple Squares. Cut them into 12 servings a tray. Placed each individual serving into a sandwich bag (not good for freezing, but read on) and placed them in the freezer. Once frozen I put them all into a couple of large freezer bags and voila! Individual bits of heaven whenever you want them. Once they are thawed I heat them up just a tad and garnish with a scoop of ice cream or a dollop of whipped cream. I guarantee that I will be making these for years to come.  Thank you BarbiAnn.

These were fabulous.  I had actually had them before when a friend made them and brought them to a pot luck.  I was impressed by their brownie-like texture, as most other "apple brownie" recipes come out cake-like when I make them.  I doubled the recipe and baked in a 7 1/2" x 11" pan, used half whole wheat flour (out of necessity - was low on all-purpose) and added an extra 1/2 tsp cinnamon and a 1/4 tsp nutmeg.  These are to die for.  Taste even better the next day, plus they freeze beautifully.  Dough is a bit sticky to work with - I pressed it into the pan with wet hands.  But totally worth it!

text:
The basic recipe is pretty good, but I would not make it again without several changes.  After seeing how tiny the amount of batter was, I tripled the recipe (except topping) as many reviewers suggested.  I used a mixture of Macintosh and Cortland apples, less sugar as suggested by other reviewers, and baked it in a 13x9 pan with the topping, for about 40 minutes.  

I did not find that the topping fell off, but the cake itself lacked flavor.  It was plenty apple-y but needs way more than the amount of cinnamon suggested here.  I actually used more cinnamon than called for, plus extra nutmeg and ginger, but it was still a little bland.  If I make it again I will definitely triple the recipe again, using only about 3/4 cup of sugar total, and add in quite a bit more spice.  Instead of the streusel topping I would frost it with a cream cheese frosting.

Doubled the recipe, except left the sugars as is (1/2 cup each). Added nutmeg. Added another cup of apple. Baked in a 9x11 pan (altered a 9x13) --- it's hard to spread. They rise and get puffy, nice thick bars.  Those who say they are "too doughy and raw" might be sifting flour and then measuring out a cup. I spoon flour into the cup and level off. Mine aren't too doughy, cooked through, and very moist. I used a combo of cortland apples diced up in 1/2 chunks and half a granny smith apple in a fine dice. Didn't top w/ cinnamon sugar but will instead make a vanilla powdered sugar thick glaze.

I received many compliments from my co-workers for baking these Apple Squares. I doubled the recipe (except the cinnamon and sugar  for the topping) and baked it in a 9x13" pan for 33 minutes. As suggested by other reviewers, I used both cinnamon and pumpkin pie spices, increased the amount of chopped apples (2 medium Granny Smith apples-about 2 1/4 cups for the doubled recipe), and sprinkled the pecans on top. The next time I bake these, I will decrease the white sugar to half as they were just a tad sweet for me!  Great recipe and worth a 5 star status!!

Delicious!  Double the recipe, and put all the dough in a 9 x 13 pan lined with parchment paper.  I didn't change any of the ingredients.  Baking takes about 35 minutes, sometimes a little longer.  I would worry more about under baking them (too gooey) than over baking (a little chewy if over baked) Made these twice in one week they were so good.  Without a doubt will make again soon. I prefere them sprinkled on top..which is what I will do next time.  oh soo good.

I made this exactly as written, except I left out the walnuts (I would have added them, but I didn't have any and it's a snowy day here).  I was worried because the batter seemed very, very thick and I had difficulty spreading it out in the 9x9 pan.  It didn't look like there was enough batter. This will be a frequently made recipe in my house--we always have the ingredients.

text:
I have made these bars with apples, raspberries and gooseberries, and I wouldn't recommend substituting the apples. The apple version was great, the others tasted funny. I'd recommend replacing at least half the all-purpose flour with whole-wheat flour and reducing the white sugar. I also found that toasting the chopped nuts before adding them to the mixture makes the bars more flavorful. Good recipe, and easy to make.

Loved these apple bars. I left out the nuts (personal preference), used a 9x13 and doubled the recipe EXCEPT the cinnamon/sugar topping which I kept the same for the first batch I made. I felt like that was still too much topping for me (and I'm a big ol' fan of sweets!). So on my next double batch, I just sprinkled on the topping until it covered the surface of the bars in a thin layer. It ended up being only about 2/3 of it, which was ideal to me. With that change, it's a keeper--disappeared in my office in record time!

text:
I took the advice of several other reviewers and doubled everything but the topping and baked it in a 9x13" pan. I am glad I didn't double the topping. As it was, I used only half of it, as it would've been overwhelmingly cinnamon-y if I'd used it all (I just sprinkled it on until the top was totally covered and then stopped). I had no walnuts so I used pecans instead and they worked great! I think I might prefer them to walnuts in this recipe, actually. It might be a little dough-y and chewy, but I think that's how it is supposed to be. I don't get the idea that this is meant to be a cake. It looks and tastes like an apple pan cookie to me.

I used whole wheat pastry flour, real butter, and omitted the nuts because we aren't big fans of them in baked goods.  Instead of the cinnamon/sugar topping, I used a struesel that I always keep on hand in the freezer (1 cup brown sugar, 1 cup quick cooking oats, 1/2 cup flour, 1/2 cup butter, some cinnamon and cut butter into dry ingredients) to top it with.  Oh, and I used pear instead of apple that I just grated to save lots of time.  They are delicious, but a bit sweet.  Next time (probably again this week!) I will try using less sugar in the batter and still top them with the streusel.  These are delicious and I know my kids are going to polish these off.

text:
In all fairness, I was unable to rate this based on the exact recipe as given due to an extreme number of food intolerances in my 10 yo, but with all of the adjustments I did for this, it turned out wonderful!  I might tweek it some, but I think it was because of my adjustments, not the original, or it wouldn't have turned out as great as it did!  It was devoured in an afternoon!  fyi, here were my adjustments: replaced flour with gluten-free mix of flours, replaced baking powder with 1/2 tsp baking soda and 1/4 tsp cream of tartar (corn intol. so no baking powder 'cause it uses cornstarch), replaced butter w/melted palm oil "ethical" veg shortening ('cause dairy intol), and replaced egg with 1 T flax see and 3 T water (egg intol).  Also added 3/4 tsp xanthum gum and 1/4 tsp baking soda due to use of gf flours.

I tried this out yesterday for a Memorial Day BBQ. I had a bag of Mcintosh apples that I needed to use, so chopped those up with one granny smith and it worked really well! Looks are deceiving - this dessert looks average, but once you pop one into your mouth, you are a true convert. text:
This was my first time making this recipe. I read reviews and decided to double the recipe and add a tad more apples (like 1/2 cup more diced apple). First, the "batter" was so thick I added about 1-2T of tart cherry juice. I did not add the sugar on top - I only added some cinnamon. I used a 9"x9" square pan baked at 350. My issues with this recipe are; (1) with the doubling in that pan it took nearly an hour to bake and i had ot put aluminum foil to keep the to from burning (which worked wonderfully), (2) It was too sweet for my taste. i like sweet things in general, but I used Jonagolds and the cake was just too sweet, (3) It was too "cakey" I thought it would be more dense and bar-like but it was more cake-like and I was disappointed. They aren't horrible and I am sure my hubby will eat them as will I but if I attempt this recipe again, I will certainly need to make a lot of changes.

text:
Very good! I was looking for a quick, "fallish" afternoon snack to make today, and this fit the bill perfectly! I followed BarbiAnn's directions exactly, except for omitting the walnuts (I only had  pecans on hand and didn't feel they would be a good substitute) and using about 3/4 cups worth of GrannySmith apple (my large apple was well over a 1/2 cup's worth; I realized that half of it would suffice, but decided to add a tad more - and then eat the rest!). I used my 9 inch Pampered Chef stoneware baking dish for this and baked for a total of 27.5 minutes. I still think I could have baked longer, but the top was VERY brown so I decided not to.... My only suggestions (for next time!) are to double the recipe (not the topping tho) and cover with foil to prevent excessive browning. I think with these changes, my bars would turn out even better! As is, they are just too thin (IMHO) and don't hold up well once cut (they crumble easily), but that's a minor complaint that can easily be corrected by doubling the batter. Thanks for sharing your idea, Barbi :)

text:
I made these after getting a little ambitious about my baking with apples & purchased near 20 lbs. of apples from my local orchard. These are delightful! I changed a few things and added some other's suggestions- I subbed pecans for walnuts (just as tasty), used the cinnamon/sugar topping and made a butterscotch reduction (as suggested above) with 2 T. each of brown sugar, cream, butter, and what teeny bit of vanilla extract I had left. They came out great- gooey/cakey with the crunchy sugar topping & gooey butterscotch/caramel on top- they are not overly sweet, which is also nice. These would make a nice light dessert or go wonderfully paired with coffee in the morning.

Four stars good. I wasn't as impressed with these as some of the reviewers who rated it more highly. They were good, but I doubled the recipe (as is just doesn't make enough). Even doubling, I thought it necessary to add an extra 2/3 cup of chopped apple (I used Braeburns). 1 cup of apples (1/2 cup in the original recipe), just didn't seem enough. And still the squares came out on the dry side. Maybe the poster should ammend her advice about waiting until they bounce back before taking out of the oven, or perhaps oven temp is too high? They can probably come out a few minutes earlier, and next time (yes I will make these again, they were, overall very good, just not what I expected) I will add more apples also. The recipe doesn't specify whether apples should be peeled first before chopping. I peeled mine, maybe that's the issue?? Did anyone else find these a tad on the dry side?

text:
These are excellent, but I do feel they are more of a coffee cake texture than an actual square/bar texture. Unlike most reviewers, I made the original recipe for a small square pan. Per reviews, I made the following modifications and was very pleased with the result. 1.) I cut back the sugar to 1/3 cup for each the white and brown sugar 2.) I used an entire apple, about 1 full cup and left out the nuts 3.) I didn't make the full cinnamon/sugar topping amount. They turned out very moist and everyone loved them. They are extremely easy to make and I will definitely make them again. Excellent for either a dessert or breakfast item.

text:
These were a very yummy treat, but with a few changes, they could be 5 star!  I made the recipe exactly as stated.  They really are PLENTY sweet without even adding the sugar topping.  I added it, but it just seemed to kind of bake into the top of the bars - no real topping.  Next time I will definitely totally leave off the sugar topping, and probably even drop the white sugar in the bars down to 1/4 cup.  The spice and apple tastes are so delicious, you really don't need all of the excess sweetness.  The only other change I would make is to increase the apple amount, and be sure to chop them into very small pieces so that you don't end up with sort of mushy big chunks in your finished product.  Overall, a tasty recipe to try, and a great addition (with changes!) to my collection - Thanks!
